Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazili objection is logically sound and shows that speech cannot be an attribute of God.
Correction: Nasafi demonstrates that the objection is based on obfuscation and self-contradiction; speech can be an attribute if the subject receives it, and God's speech must be eternal.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what determines whether a subject can be described by an attribute?
A) Whether the attribute is essential or accidental
B) Whether the attribute can possibly exist in the subject
C) Whether the attribute is created or eternal
D) Whether the subject is animate or inanimate

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazili objection by showing that a subject can be described by an attribute if the attribute can exist in it, and he proves God's speech must be eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear an objection against Islamic beliefs that sounds logical, do you instinctively accept it because it appeals to your intellect, or do you pause to examine whether it is based on sound principles? This lesson shows that even seemingly coherent arguments can collapse when their own assumptions are turned against them. Will you commit to not accepting any objection without first seeking the full scholarly refutation?
?
The Mu'tazila turned away from following the clear proof (السبيل) and ended up in bewilderment. Are there areas in your life where you have relied on your own reasoning over clear revelation—perhaps in matters of faith, morality, or daily decisions? What step will you take today to realign yourself with the guidance of Allah and His Messenger?
?
Nasafi uses a simple analogy of a sleeping person to dismantle a major objection. How often do you dismiss the proofs of Islamic theology as 'too difficult' or 'irrelevant' without realizing that they are designed to address your deepest doubts? Will you make a sincere effort to study even one attribute of Allah with the same depth this lesson offers, and let it transform your worship?

Rational Proof for the Eternity of Allah's Speech
Nasafi gives a rational proof for the eternity of Allah's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's rational argument that Allah's speech must be eternal, based on the impossibility of change or imperfection in the divine essence.

Core Idea
Allah cannot be silent or impeded; therefore He has always been speaking.

This passage presents a key rational proof from Imam al-Nasafi in the Maturidi tradition. The argument uses a reductio ad absurdum to show that if Allah were not speaking in pre-eternity, He would have to be silent or have an impediment—both impossible for the Eternal. Let's trace the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
Recognize that Allah is a living being perfectly capable of speech. The argument begins from this fact.
The premise is that Allah is 'alive' and speech is a possible attribute for Him.
2
Consider the alternatives
If Allah were not speaking in pre-eternity, He would necessarily be described by one of the opposites of speech: silence or an impediment like dumbness. Note that for a living being capable of speech, the absence of speech must have a cause.
The author mentions 'silence' (sukūt) and 'impediment' (āfa).
3
Examine why each alternative is impossible
Impediments like dumbness are marks of origination (ḥudūth) and cannot apply to the Eternal. Silence, if by essence, would prevent speech forever; if by a reason, that reason would be an impediment—again impossible. Therefore, the only possibility is that Allah has always been speaking.
The argument concludes that speech must be eternal, though the text cuts off mid-sentence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل عقلي آخر على قدم كلام الله: ومعقول آخر لنا في المسألة أنه تعالى لو لم يكن في الأزل متكلما لكان موصوفا بضد من أضداد الكلام كالسكوت، والآفة، لأن الحي الذي لا يستحيل أن يكون متكلما لم يتعر عنه، لاقتضاء الذات التعري، إذ لو كان كذلك لما تصور الاتصاف بالكلام البتة لاستحالة التغير على الذات، وخروجه عن كونه مقتضيا ما كان يقتضيه في الأزل، فلو كان متعريا لكان لقيام ضد من أضداده به يمنع ذلك قبول الاتصاف بالكلام، وهذا محال لأن الآفة كالخرس والطفولية وغيرهما على القديم ممتنعة إذ هي من أمارات الحدوث، وكذا السكوت عنه في الأزل منتفي، فإنه لو كان ساكتا في الأزل لكان لا يتصور اتصافه بالكلام البتة لأن الأمر لا يخلو إما أن كان ساكتا لذاته، وإما أن كان ساكتا لمعنى، والاتصاف بالكلام مع وجود ما
Another rational proof for the eternity of the speech of Allah: And another intelligible [argument] for us on the issue: that if He, exalted, were not speaking in pre-eternity, He would be described by an opposite of the opposites of speech, like silence or impediment, because a living being which is not impossible to be a speaker is not devoid of them, due to the essence requiring non-devoidance [of speech or its opposite]. For if it were otherwise, then description by speech could not be conceived at all due to the impossibility of change upon the essence and its departing from being productive of what it was productive of in pre-eternity. And if it were devoid, then it would be due to the subsistence of an opposite of its opposites in it, preventing that acceptance of description by speech. And this is impossible because impediments like dumbness, infancy, and others are impossible for the Eternal, since they are marks of origination. And likewise, silence regarding Him in pre-eternity is negated. For if He were silent in pre-eternity, then His description by speech could not be conceived at all, because the matter is either that He was silent by His essence, or that He was silent due to a reason. And description by speech with the existence of what...
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage presents a rational proof for the eternity of Allah's speech (kalām). The proof is structured as a reductio ad absurdum. The author argues: If Allah were not speaking in pre-eternity (al-azal), then He would necessarily be described by one of the opposites of speech, such as silence (sukūt) or an impediment (āfa) like dumbness. Why? Because a living being that can possibly speak cannot be devoid of both speech and its opposites without a cause—its nature demands either speech or its opposite. If Allah were devoid of any such attribute, then He could never acquire speech later, because that would entail change (taghayyur) in the divine essence, which is impossible. Moreover, if He were not speaking due to the presence of an opposite, that opposite would prevent speech. But an impediment like dumbness or infancy is impossible for the Eternal, as they are marks of origination (ḥudūth). Similarly, silence in pre-eternity is negated, because if He were silent by essence, He could never speak; if by a reason, that reason would be an impediment, which is impossible. The argument concludes that Allah must have been speaking in pre-eternity, thus His speech is eternal. Note: The text cuts off at the end, but the logical structure is clear: the only remaining possibility is that Allah is eternally speaking.

Key Terms
أزل (pre-eternity)
متكلما (speaking)
سكوت (silence)
آفة (impediment)
تغير (change)
صفة (attribute)
حدوث (origination)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Silence is a neutral state that does not require a cause.
Correction: Nasafi argues that for a living being capable of speech, the absence of speech implies an active state (silence or impediment) which must have a reason, leading to impossibility for Allah.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's proof, why is silence in pre-eternity impossible for Allah?
A) Because silence is a kind of impediment.
B) Because silence would be either by essence or by a reason, and both prevent speech eternally or entail impediment.
C) Because silence is a created attribute.
D) Because Allah is always speaking.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is eternal because any alternative—silence or impediment—implies change or imperfection, which cannot apply to the Divine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that Allah's speech is eternal—He has always been speaking. Yet how often do you go through your days without giving ear to His speech? If He were silent even for a moment, what would be the consequence for your soul? Commit today to a fixed time for listening to His words in the Quran, as if your life depends on it—because it does.
?
The proof shows that silence in Allah is impossible because it implies change or defect. But you often choose silence when you should speak the truth, excusing yourself by your weakness. Are you not, in those moments, acting as if Allah could be silent about your sin? How will you break that silence this week?
?
If Allah had an impediment like dumbness, He would be imperfect—but He is perfect in every attribute. Yet you sometimes doubt that His speech is sufficient for all your needs. What specific need or anxiety have you been ignoring from His book? Write it down and commit to finding the verse that addresses it.

A Second Rational Proof for the Eternity of Allah's Speech
Imam al-Nasafi presents a second rational proof that Allah's speech is eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second rational proof for the eternity of Allah's speech (kalam), based on the impossibility of change or defect in the Eternal.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is eternal because the alternative—silence or defect—is impossible for the Eternal.

Imam al-Nasafi presents another rational argument that complements the first. This proof uses a disjunctive syllogism: either Allah was speaking in pre-eternity or He was not. By eliminating all alternatives, we arrive at the necessary conclusion that His speech is eternal. Let's trace the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the disjunctive premise
The argument starts with a clear either/or: either Allah was speaking in pre-eternity or He was not. If He was not, He must be described with an opposite of speech (silence or defect).
This is a classic kalam disjunction.
2
Examine why defect is impossible
Defects like muteness or infancy are signs of origination (huduth) and therefore cannot apply to the Eternal.
The Eternal is not subject to change or imperfection.
3
Examine why silence is impossible
If Allah were silent in pre-eternity, it would be either by His essence or due to a meaning. Both options require change or a defect, which are impossible for the Eternal.
This eliminates the second alternative.
4
Conclude that Allah must be speaking
Since both opposites are impossible, and there is no intermediate state between speech and its opposites, Allah must be speaking eternally.
The conclusion is necessary.
5
Connect to the materialist claim
The proof also argues that if stripping of speech were possible, it would support the materialist claim that atoms can be stripped of accidents, leading to the world's eternity—which is false.
This strengthens the argument by showing its broader implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعقول آخر لنا في المسألة أنه تعالى لو لم يكن في الأزل متكلما لكان موصوفا بضد من أضداد الكلام كالسكوت، والآفة، لأن الحي الذي لا يستحيل أن يكون متكلما لم يتعر عنه، لاقتضاء الذات التعري، إذ لو كان كذلك لما تصور الاتصاف بالكلام البتة لاستحالة التغير على الذات، وخروجه عن كونه مقتضيا ما كان يقتضيه في الأزل، فلو كان متعريا لكان لقيام ضد من أضداده به يمنع ذلك قبول الاتصاف بالكلام، وهذا محال لأن الآفة كالخرس والطفولية وغيرهما على القديم ممتنعة إذ هي من أمارات الحدوث، وكذا السكوت عنه في الأزل منتفي، فإنه لو كان ساكتا في الأزل لكان لا يتصور اتصافه بالكلام البتة لأن الأمر لا يخلو إما أن كان ساكتا لذاته، وإما أن كان ساكتا لمعنى، والاتصاف بالكلام مع وجود ما اتصافه يوجب ذاتا كان أو معنى لما مر من إحالة العدم على القديم، وإذا لم يكن في الأزل موصوفا بضد من أضداد الكلام ولا يستحيل اتصاف الذات بالكلام، كان موصوفا به ضرورة، إذ لا واسطة في حق ما يصح اتصافه بالكلام، بين الكلام وأضداده، فيستحيل التعري. لو هذا كان تعري الجواهر عن الأعراض على حسب ما يزعمه أهل الدهر مستحيلا لما مر من المعنى، ولو جاز التعري فيما نحن فيه، لجاز هناك، وصح القول بقدم العالم وهذا باطل، فكذا هذا، ولهذا لم يكن في الشاهد ما يصح اتصافه بالكلام متعريا عنه إلا إذا وجد ضد من أضداده قائما به. والله الموفق. بالسكوت محال ممتنع والعدم على ما يوجب كونه ساكتا محال
And there is another rational argument for us on the matter: that if the Exalted were not speaking in pre-eternity, He would be described with an opposite of the opposites of speech, such as silence or defect, because the living being which is not impossible to be speaking is not stripped of it [speech], due to the essence requiring stripping, for if it were so, then being described with speech would not be conceivable at all due to the impossibility of change upon the essence, and its departure from being what necessitates what it used to necessitate in pre-eternity. So if it were stripped, then because an opposite from its opposites stands in it, that would prevent the acceptance of being described with speech, and this is impossible because a defect like muteness, infancy, and others is impossible for the Eternal, as they are signs of origination. Likewise, silence is negated from Him in pre-eternity, for if He were silent in pre-eternity, then His being described with speech would not be conceivable at all, because the matter is not free from either He is silent by His essence or He is silent due to a meaning, and being described with speech while that exists which necessitates His being described with either essence or meaning is impossible due to what has passed of the impossibility of non-existence upon the Eternal. And when He is not described in pre-eternity with any opposite of the opposites of speech, and it is not impossible for the essence to be described with speech, then He is necessarily described with it, for there is no intermediate state regarding what is valid to be described with speech between speech and its opposites, so stripping is impossible. If stripping were possible here, then the stripping of atoms from accidents would be possible as the materialists claim, due to the same meaning, and the statement of the world's pre-eternity would be valid, and this is false, so likewise this is false. Therefore, in the witnessed world, nothing that is valid to be described with speech is stripped of it unless an opposite from its opposites stands in it. And Allah is the Grantor of success. Silence is impossible and impossible, and non-existence upon what necessitates his being silent is impossible.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage presents a second rational proof for the eternity of Allah's speech (kalam). The argument follows a disjunctive syllogism: either Allah was speaking in pre-eternity (azal) or He was not. If He was not speaking, then He must have been described with one of the opposites of speech, such as silence or a defect (like muteness). The proof proceeds by showing that both alternatives are impossible for the Eternal. First, defects are signs of origination (huduth) and thus impossible for the Eternal. Second, silence is also impossible because if He were silent in pre-eternity, it would be either by His essence or due to a meaning. If by essence, then change would be needed to become speaking, but change is impossible for the Eternal. If due to a meaning, then that meaning would be a defect or a quality that prevents speech, which is also impossible. Therefore, since the Eternal cannot have any opposite of speech, and it is not impossible for Him to be described with speech, He must be described with speech necessarily. The argument further supports this by pointing out that in the empirical world any being capable of speech is either speaking or has an opposite preventing it; there is no third state. The proof also connects this to the cosmological argument: if stripping were allowed for speech, it would allow stripping of accidents from substances, leading to the materialist claim of the world's eternity, which is false. Thus, the speech of Allah is eternal.

تعري
قديم
آفة
سكوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's speech is not eternal; He began to speak after creation.
Correction: The proof shows that if Allah were not speaking in pre-eternity, He would have an opposite like silence or defect, both impossible for the Eternal. Thus, His speech must be eternal.

Checkpoint
According to the second rational proof, why is it impossible for Allah to have been silent in pre-eternity?
A) Because silence is a defect and defects are signs of origination.
B) Because silence would imply that Allah is not omnipotent.
C) Because the Qur'an explicitly states that Allah speaks.
D) Because silence is impossible for any living being.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech must be eternal because the alternatives—silence or defect—are impossible for the Eternal, and any being capable of speech is either speaking or prevented by an opposite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's speech is eternal and unchanging, then His commands and prohibitions are not subject to revision. Does your daily obedience reflect the permanence of His speech, or do you treat some commands as outdated?
?
Imam al-Nasafi argues that silence in pre-eternity would imply a defect. Do you ever wish Allah had remained silent on certain issues so you could have more freedom? What does that say about your trust in His wisdom?
?
The proof shows that Allah cannot change from silent to speaking. When you read the Qur'an, do you truly sense that you are hearing the same eternal speech that was with Allah always, or do you unconsciously treat it as a temporal book?

Response to Mu'tazila Objection on Stripping of Opposites
Imam al-Nasafi answers the Mu'tazila objection by distinguishing between possible and impossible attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila analogy from the witnessed world fails to apply to Allah, and how the principle that a possible attribute cannot be absent without a present opposite is key.

Core Idea
A possible attribute cannot be absent without a present opposite – but that opposite must be possible for the subject.

The Mu'tazila raise an objection based on empirical observation: in the world, living beings are never stripped of certain opposite pairs (asleep/awake, etc.), yet Allah is stripped of all such opposites. So why can't He be stripped of speech and its opposites? Imam al-Nasafi answers by distinguishing between attributes that are possible for a subject and those that are impossible. The proof for speech does not rely on a general impossibility of stripping, but on the logical principle that a possible attribute cannot be negated unless its opposite exists – and that opposite must be possible for the subject.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the objection is presented and how the author begins his response with 'ما يوردون من الأسئلة...'.
The objection uses examples from the witnessed world (الشاهد).
2
Identify the two parts: objection and answer
The passage has an objection (first part) and the author's answer (remaining part). The answer clarifies the principle behind the proof.
The answer starts with 'فإنا لم نبن الكلام على إثبات استحالة التعري عن الضدين...'
3
Understand the key principle
The author states: 'ما لا يستحيل ثبوته على الذات لا ينتفي عنه إلا بثبوت ضده' – a quality that is not impossible for a subject cannot be negated except by the existence of its opposite.
This principle is the core of the response.
4
Apply the principle to the examples
See how in the witnessed world, the opposites (sleep/awake) are possible for the subject, so one is negated only when the other is present. For Allah, those opposites are impossible, so their absence is due to impossibility, not a present opposite.
The Mu'tazila assumed the same rule applies, but it does not.
5
Conclude the lesson
Conclude that the objection fails because it confuses two different cases. The proof for speech stands: speech is possible for Allah, its opposite (silence/defect) is impossible, so speech must be eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يوردون من الأسئلة على هذه الطريقة أن في الشاهد لا يتعرى الحي عن كونه نائما أو منتبها أو ولودا أو عقيما أو متحركا أو ساكنا، ومع ذلك يتعرى ذات القديم عنها كلها، فكذا يجوز أن يتعرى عن الكلام وأضداده في القدم وإن كان التعري في الشاهد غير ثابت أسئلة فاسدة غير متوجهة على ما ذكرنا، فإنا لم نبن الكلام على إثبات استحالة التعري عن الضدين في حق القديم لكون ذلك مستحيلا الشاهد بل قلنا إن ما لا يستحيل ثبوته على الذات لا ينتفي عنه إلا بثبوت ضده، والكلام من هذا القبيل، فلا ينتفي إلا بثبوت ضده، وثبوت الضد عليه محال وفيما أوردوا من الأمثلة كانت الحال في الشاهد على نحو ما بينا، فلم ينعدم أحدهما عن المحل إلا بثبوت ضده لجواز قبول المحل كل ذلك، فأما القديم تعالى فيستحيل عليه تلك الأوصاف، فانتفاء كل ضد من ذلك كان لاستحالة قبول القديم إياه، لا لوجود ضده، وفيما نحن فيه الأمر بخلافه.
And what they raise as objections upon this method: that in the witnessed world, the living being is not stripped of being sleeping or awake, or fertile or barren, or moving or still, yet the essence of the Eternal is stripped of all of them, so likewise it is permissible that He be stripped of speech and its opposites in pre-eternity, even though stripping in the witnessed world is not established. [These are] corrupt objections that are not applicable to what we have mentioned. For we did not base the argument on establishing the impossibility of stripping from the two opposites in the case of the Eternal because that is impossible in the witnessed world. Rather, we said that what is not impossible to subsist upon the essence is not negated from it except by the subsistence of its opposite, and speech is of this category. So it is not negated except by the subsistence of its opposite, and the subsistence of the opposite upon Him is impossible. And in the examples they adduced, the situation in the witnessed world is as we explained: one of the two does not cease from the substrate except by the subsistence of its opposite, because the substrate is capable of receiving all of that. As for the Eternal, the Exalted, those attributes are impossible for Him. So the negation of each opposite from that is because of the impossibility of the Eternal's receiving it, not due to the existence of its opposite. And in our case, the matter is the opposite of that.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The Mu'tazila object to the previous proof by citing empirical examples: in the witnessed world, a living being is never stripped of certain binary opposites (asleep/awake, fertile/barren, moving/still), yet Allah's essence is stripped of all those opposites (e.g., He is neither asleep nor awake). So why can't He also be stripped of speech and its opposites? The author responds by clarifying that the proof does not rely on the impossibility of stripping from opposites in general. Rather, the proof is built on the principle: a quality that is not impossible for a subject cannot be absent unless its opposite is present. Speech is such a quality for Allah (since it is not impossible for Him to speak), so it cannot be absent without a present opposite. But the opposite (silence, defect) is impossible for Allah. Therefore, speech must be present. In the examples given, the opposites are possible for the subject (e.g., a human can be asleep or awake), so one opposite is negated only when the other is present. For Allah, the opposites are impossible, so their absence is due to impossibility, not due to the presence of the opposite. Thus, the objection is invalid because it confuses two different cases.

Key Terms

تعري
ضد
قديم
استحالة
محل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since Allah is stripped of all opposites in the witnessed world (like asleep/awake), He can also be stripped of speech and its opposites.
Correction: The stripping in those examples is due to the impossibility of those attributes for Allah, not due to the presence of their opposites. For speech, the opposite is impossible, so speech must be present.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the Mu'tazila objection is invalid?
A) Because the examples they gave are not relevant to speech.
B) Because the proof did not rely on the impossibility of stripping in the witnessed world.
C) Because Allah cannot be described as awake or asleep.
D) Because the Mu'tazila reject the eternity of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The proof for the eternity of speech does not rely on a general impossibility of stripping, but on the logical necessity that a possible attribute cannot be absent without its opposite – which is impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's speech is eternal and not created, what does that mean for your relationship with the Quran? Do you approach it as the very words of the Eternal, or do you read it with the same attitude as human books? How would that change your attentiveness tonight when you recite?
?
The Mu'tazila made the mistake of assuming that because some attributes are impossible for Allah, all are—ignoring the logical difference. Where in your own thinking about Allah have you perhaps fallen into a similar error of overgeneralizing from creation to the Creator? Will you examine one specific belief today to ensure it is grounded in revelation and reason, not analogy?
?
The principle states that a possible attribute cannot be absent without its opposite. Could you say that belief in Allah's eternal speech is a 'possible attribute' of your faith—something you could lose if its opposite (doubt) takes hold? What opposite are you allowing to exist in your heart that might be pushing out the certainty that Allah speaks to you through His Book?

The Necessity of God's Attribute of Speech
Proof that God must possess speech to avoid being devoid of opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument for why God necessarily possesses the attribute of speech, based on the impossibility of being devoid of opposites.

Core Idea
If God cannot be silent, He must speak — no middle ground exists.

This lesson presents a key Maturidi proof for the divine attribute of speech. The argument hinges on a logical principle: if a being is capable of an attribute and its opposite is impossible, then the being must possess that attribute. Imam al-Nasafi applies this to God's speech, demonstrating that silence is impossible for Him, so speech is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the logical structure: the argument moves from the impossibility of non-existence for the Eternal to the impossibility of being devoid of speech and its opposites.
Pay attention to the phrase 'no intermediate state'.
2
Identify the key logical move
The author states that if in pre-eternity God was not described with any opposite of speech, and it is possible for Him to be described with speech, then He must be described with speech. There is no intermediate state.
3
Consider the analogy
The author rejects the possibility of being devoid by analogy: if allowed, it would imply atoms could be devoid of accidents, leading to the eternity of the world, which is false.
This analogy strengthens the proof from the witnessed world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اتصافه (1) يوجب ذاتا كان أو معنى لما مر من إحالة العدم على القديم، وإذا لم يكن في الأزل موصوفا بضد من أضداد الكلام ولا يستحيل اتصاف الذات بالكلام، كان موصوفا به ضرورة، إذ لا واسطة في حق ما يصح اتصافه بالكلام، بين الكلام وأضداده، فيستحيل التعري. لو هذا كان تعري الجواهر عن الأعراض على حسب ما يزعمه أهل الدهر مستحيلا لما مر من المعنى، ولو جاز التعري فيما نحن فيه، لجاز هناك، وصح القول بقدم العالم وهذا باطل، فكذا هذا، ولهذا لم يكن في الشاهد ما يصح اتصافه بالكلام متعريا عنه إلا إذا وجد ضد من أضداده قائما (2) به. والله الموفق. بالسكوت محال ممتنع والعدم على ما يوجب كونه ساكتا محال
His being described (with speech) necessitates a self or a meaning due to what has been said about the impossibility of non-existence applying to the Eternal. And if in eternity He was not described with any opposite of speech and it is not impossible for the self to be described with speech, then He is necessarily described with it, because there is no intermediate state for that which is valid to be described with speech between speech and its opposites, so being devoid is impossible. If this were not the case, then the being devoid of atoms of accidents according to what the materialists claim would be impossible for the same reason, and if being devoid were permissible in our case, it would be permissible there, and the statement of the eternity of the world would be valid, and this is false. So likewise this is false. For this reason, in the witnessed world, nothing that is valid to be described with speech is devoid of it unless one of its opposites exists in it. And God is the giver of success. Silence is impossible and non-existent, and that which would necessitate him being silent is impossible.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the necessity of God's attribute of speech (kalam). The argument proceeds from the impossibility of being devoid of both a thing and its opposite when the thing is possible and the opposite is impossible. The author states: if a being is capable of speech and its opposite (e.g., silence) is impossible for that being, then the being must be described with speech. He supports this with an analogy: if being devoid were allowed, it would imply the possibility of atoms being devoid of accidents, leading to the eternity of the world, which is false. In the witnessed world (al-shahid), any being capable of speech is never devoid of speech or its opposite; thus, for God, who cannot have the opposite, speech is necessary. The final line emphasizes that silence is impossible for God.

Misconception: God could be devoid of speech and its opposite, remaining neutral.
Correction: The argument proves that for a being capable of speech, being devoid of both speech and its opposite is impossible; there is no intermediate state. Since silence is impossible for God, speech is necessary.

D) Because the Qur'an says so.

Key Takeaway
God's attribute of speech is necessary because silence is impossible for Him and being devoid of both is logically impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Refuting the Mu'tazila Objection on the Speech Argument
Refutation of Mu'tazila objection using examples from the witnessed world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila analogy from the witnessed world fails to disprove God's speech, and how the impossibility of opposites leads to the necessity of speech.

Core Idea
What is impossible for God cannot be used to argue against what is possible.

The Mu'tazila object that just as a living being can be devoid of both sleep and wakefulness, God could be devoid of speech and its opposite. In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi refutes this by distinguishing between attributes that are impossible for God and those that are possible. He shows that speech, being a perfection, cannot be negated without an impossible opposite.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila objection
Read the opening lines describing the Mu'tazila analogy: in the witnessed world, a living being can lack both opposites (e.g., sleep and wake), so why can't God lack speech and its opposite?
The objection seems plausible, but the author will expose its flaw.
2
Grasp the key distinction
Notice how the author distinguishes between attributes that are impossible for God (like sleep) and those that are possible for God (like speech). The absence of impossible attributes does not require an opposite; their absence is due to impossibility.
This distinction is crucial to the refutation.
3
See how the argument forces affirmation of speech
The author argues that speech, being a possible perfection, cannot be negated except by the existence of its opposite. Since the opposite (silence?) is impossible for God, speech must exist. Trace this reasoning step by step.
This is the heart of the argument for the attribute of speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتراض للمعتزلة] وما يوردون من الأسئلة على هذه الطريقة أن في الشاهد لا يتعرى الحي عن كونه نائما أو منتبها أو ولودا أو عقيما أو متحركا أو ساكنا، ومع ذلك يتعرى ذات القديم عنها كلها، فكذا يجوز أن يتعرى عن الكلام وأضداده في القدم وإن كان التعري في الشاهد غير ثابت أسئلة فاسدة غير متوجهة على ما ذكرنا، فإنا لم نبن الكلام على إثبات استحالة التعري عن الضدين في حق القديم لكون ذلك مستحيلا الشاهد بل قلنا إن ما لا يستحيل ثبوته على الذات لا ينتفي عنه إلا بثبوت ضده، والكلام من هذا القبيل، فلا ينتفي إلا بثبوت ضده، وثبوت الضد عليه محال وفيما (3) أوردوا من الأمثلة كانت الحال في الشاهد على نحو ما بينا، فلم ينعدم أحدهما عن المحل إلا بثبوت ضده لجواز قبول المحل كل ذلك، فأما القديم تعالى فيستحيل عليه تلك الأوصاف، فانتفاء كل ضد من ذلك كان لاستحالة قبول القديم إياه، لا لوجود ضده، وفيما نحن فيه الأمر بخلافه.
An objection of the Mu'tazila: And what they raise as questions on this method: that in the witnessed world, the living being is not devoid of being asleep or awake, or fertile or barren, or moving or still, yet the Eternal Self is devoid of all of them. So likewise it is permissible that He be devoid of speech and its opposites in eternity, even if being devoid in the witnessed world is not established. These are corrupt questions that are not directed at what we mentioned. For we did not base the speech on establishing the impossibility of being devoid of both opposites regarding the Eternal because that is impossible in the witnessed world. Rather we said: that which its existence on the self is not impossible is not negated from it except by the existence of its opposite. And speech is of this kind, so it is not negated except by the existence of its opposite, and the existence of the opposite upon Him is impossible. And in the examples they brought, the situation in the witnessed world is as we explained, for one of the two is not absent from the locus except by the existence of its opposite, due to the permissibility of the locus accepting all of that. As for the Eternal, Exalted, those attributes are impossible for Him, so the negation of each opposite from that was due to the impossibility of the Eternal accepting it, not due to the existence of its opposite. And in our case, the matter is contrary to that.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The Mu'tazila object that in the witnessed world, a living being can be devoid of many pairs of opposites (e.g., sleep/wakefulness) without having either, so why can't God be devoid of speech and its opposites? The author replies that the objection is invalid because those attributes (sleep, wakefulness, etc.) are impossible for God, so their absence is due to impossibility, not due to the presence of an opposite. Speech, however, is a possible attribute for God, and its opposite is impossible; therefore, God must have speech. The author distinguishes between attributes that are possible for a being and those that are not.

Key Terms
الشاهد
الضدان
المحل
القديم
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God can be devoid of some opposites (like sleep/wake), He can be devoid of all opposites, including speech.
Correction: The attributes in the examples are impossible for God; their absence is due to impossibility, not the presence of an opposite. Speech is possible, so its absence would require an impossible opposite.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the Mu'tazila's comparison of God to a living being that is devoid of sleep and wakefulness?
A) Because God is not like a living being.
B) Because sleep and wakefulness are impossible for God, so their absence is different.
C) Because the living being actually has one of the opposites.
D) Because the Mu'tazila are wrong.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is necessary because its opposite is impossible, unlike contingent attributes that are impossible for Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a truth about Allah because you thought, 'If He can lack this, He can lack that' without examining the underlying logical principles? Will you now test your assumptions against the principle of impossibility of opposites, even when it challenges your comfort?
?
The Mu'tazila insisted on measuring the unseen by the seen. Where in your own life do you impose worldly criteria on the Divine—perhaps expecting Allah to act like a human ruler or judge? Are you willing to submit to what reason and revelation demand, even if it feels unfamiliar or humbling?
?
The author argues that what is not impossible for God cannot be negated without an impossible opposite. Reflect on an attribute of Allah (e.g., His mercy, His justice) that you might have doubted or minimized because you could not see its opposite. How does this principle compel you to reaffirm it?

Refutation of the Objection Regarding 'Adl and Tafaddul
Maturidi response to Ash'ari-denied eternal attributes objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi position on the eternality of God's attributes of action (like justice and beneficence) avoids objections that apply to the Ash'ari position.

Core Idea
God's justice is eternal — only then does the objection vanish.

The objectors claim that God can be described as just without having its opposite (injustice) in eternity. This objection, however, only holds against the Ash'ari, who deny that attributes like justice are eternal. For Maturidis, God is eternally just and munificent, so the opposite never arises. This passage clarifies the doctrinal difference and defends the Maturidi view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the two parallel objections about justice and beneficence.
The passage is dense with theological positions; read slowly.
2
Identify the Ash'ari vulnerability
Notice that the objection only binds the Ash'ari because they deny attributes of action in eternity. Understand why this makes their position susceptible.
The Ash'ari hold that attributes like 'just' are not eternal but arise with creation.
3
Contrast the Maturidi position
The Maturidis affirm that God is eternally just and munificent. See how this directly answers the objection: if the attribute is eternal, its opposite never has a place.
This is the core of the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يزعمون أن الله تعالى لا يستحيل أن يوصف بكونه عادلا ثم في الأزل كان غير موصوف به ولم يلزم اتصافه بضده وهو الجور. سؤال يلزم الأشعري لمطابقتهم إياه على انتفاء صفات الفعل في الأزل فأما علينا فغير لازم، لأنه تعالى عندنا كان في الأزل موصوفا بالعدل. وكذا ما يزعمون أنه تعالى لو لم يكن في الأزل متفضلا لكان بخيلا من هذا القبيل. فإنه عندنا في الأزل كان متفضلا، وإنما يتوجه هذا السؤال على الأشعري (1).
And what they claim: that God, Exalted, is not impossible to be described as 'just', yet in eternity He was not described with it, and it does not necessitate that He be described with its opposite, which is injustice. This question is binding upon the Ash'ari, because they agreed with them on the negation of the attributes of action in eternity. As for us, it is not binding, because He, Exalted, according to us, was in eternity described with justice. Likewise, what they claim: that if He, Exalted, was not in eternity munificent, He would be miserly, is of this kind. For according to us, He was in eternity munificent, and this question only applies to the Ash'ari.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. The objectors argue that God can be just without having its opposite (injustice) in eternity. The author points out that this objection applies only to the Ash'ari, who deny that attributes like justice are eternal (considering them attributes of action). For Maturidis, God is eternally described with justice and munificence (tafaddul). Therefore, the opposite never occurs, and the objection does not apply to them.

Key Terms

الجور
التفضل
البخل

الأشعري

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's justice and beneficence are not eternal attributes; that denying their eternality does not lead to their opposites.
Correction: The Maturidi position affirms that God is eternally just and munificent, thus precluding the possibility of their opposites (injustice and miserliness). The objection only applies to those who deny eternal attributes of action, like the Ash'ari.

Checkpoint

A) They deny God is just.
B) They affirm God is eternally just.
C) They say God is not described with justice.
D) They follow the Ash'ari.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi affirmation of God's eternal justice and beneficence shields them from objections that target the Ash'ari denial of eternal attributes of action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

But have you truly internalized that God's justice and generosity are not new qualities—they are who He has always been? How should that reshape your worship and reliance on Him starting now?

Refutation of the Objection About the Capable Being Devoid of Speech
Refutation of claim that a capable being can be devoid of speech and its opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi response to the objection that a capable being can be devoid of speech and its opposites, and how they critique the Mu'tazili position.

Core Idea
Ability (qudra) in God is concurrent with the act, not prior.

This passage addresses a key objection raised by the Mu'tazila regarding God's speech. They claimed that since a human can be capable of speech yet remain silent, God could also be capable of speech without actually speaking. The Maturidi response refutes this by clarifying the relationship between ability and its object, and by turning the argument back on the Mu'tazila using their own principles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two positions
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Identify the Mu'tazili claim and the Maturidi response. Notice how the author starts by stating the objection.
The objection is based on the principle that ability precedes the act.
2
Understand the Maturidi principle of concurrency
Focus on the phrase 'فالقدرة على الكلام، مقترنة بالكلام' (ability for speech is concurrent with speech). This is the key doctrine. Ask yourself how this differs from the Mu'tazili view.
For Maturidis, if a being has ability, the act must be present or its opposite.
3
See how the argument is turned against the Mu'tazila
The author says that even on Mu'tazili principles, ability for speech does not preclude silence. They admit a silent person is capable of speech. So they cannot claim the capable being is devoid of both speech and its opposites.
This is a refutation using their own logic.
4
Apply to divine attributes
Reflect on why this matters for God: His attributes like speech are eternal and actual. The concurrency principle ensures that God is always speaking, which is necessary for His perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يزعمون أن القادر على الكلام في الشاهد يتعرى عن الكلام وأضداده في حالة ثبوت القدرة. فشيء يبنونه على أصلهم في ادعائهم سبق القدرة على المقدور فأما عندنا فالقدرة على الكلام، مقترنة بالكلام فلا يتصور التعري عنه مع وجوده، وقبل وجود القدرة كان ضدا من أضداد الكلام ثابتا . ثم يقال لهم : هذا أيضا على أصلكم فاسد ، فإن عندكم القدرة على الكلام، إن كانت منافية للآفة فهي غير منافية للسكوت، بل الساكت عندكم (3) قادر على الكلام، وهذا لأن القدرة على أحد المتضادين عندكم لا تضاد ضد مقدوره، كما في قدرة الحركة والسكون ، وقدرة الكفر والإيمان (3) وأشباه ذلك (4). وبالله التوفيق.
And what they claim: that the one who is capable of speech in the witnessed world is devoid of speech and its opposites in a state of the existence of ability. This is something they build on their principle in their claim of the precedence of ability over the power's object. As for us, ability for speech is concurrent with speech, so being devoid of it in its presence is inconceivable, and before the existence of ability, one of the opposites of speech was existing. Then it is said to them: This is also corrupt according to your principle, for according to you, ability for speech, if it is incompatible with defect, it is not incompatible with silence. Rather, according to you, the silent person is capable of speech. And this is because ability for one of two opposites according to you does not oppose the opposite of its object, as in the ability for movement and stillness, and ability for disbelief and faith, and similar things. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objectors claim that a capable person can be devoid of speech and its opposites even while having ability. The author responds that this is based on the Mu'tazila principle that ability precedes the act. For Maturidis, ability is concurrent with the act, so if the person has the ability, they must be speaking or have its opposite. The author then turns the argument against the Mu'tazila themselves: on their own principles, ability for speech does not preclude silence; they admit that a silent person can be capable of speech. Therefore, they cannot claim that the capable person is devoid of both speech and its opposites.

الكلام
السكوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ability can exist without the act in God as it does in humans.
Correction: In Maturidi theology, ability (qudra) is concurrent with the act, especially in God. God's attributes like speech are eternal and actual; He is always speaking.

Checkpoint

A) Ability precedes the act.
B) Ability is simultaneous with the act.
C) Ability follows the act.
D) Ability is independent of the act.

Key Takeaway
In Maturidi theology, ability (qudra) is concurrent with the act, so God's attributes like speech are eternally actual; He is always speaking.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
You have the ability to speak truth or remain silent. This passage shows that silence does not remove capability. When you stay silent in the face of falsehood, are you acknowledging your ability or denying it? What will you choose to do with your speech today?

Abu al-Husayn's Objection on Muteness
Abu al-Husayn's objection that muteness is not an opposite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu al-Husayn al-Basri's objection that muteness is a defect of the speech organ, not an opposite of speech, and why this matters for the argument about divine speech.

Core Idea
Muteness is a broken instrument, not the opposite of speech.

Abu al-Husayn al-Basri challenges a key premise in the argument about divine speech. He claims that muteness and silence are not genuine opposites of speech but rather a corruption of the speech organ. This objection, if accepted, would alter how we reason about God's attributes. Let's examine his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

3
Consider the implications
Why does this distinction matter? If muteness is not an opposite, then the argument that God must speak because He is not mute loses force.
This objection opens a discussion on how to properly define opposites.

Refuting Objections on Justice and Favor in Pre-Eternity
Nasafi refutes two objections about God's justice and favor in pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidis affirm that God is eternally just and generous, and why the objections of opponents only apply to the Ash'ari position.

Core Idea
God's justice and favor are eternal in Maturidi theology, not temporal.

In this passage, Nasafi addresses two objections raised against the Maturidi view of God's attributes. Opponents argue that if God is just, then in pre-eternity He must have been just, but they deny that attributes of action are eternal. Nasafi shows that this objection only holds for the Ash'ari who negate such attributes, whereas Maturidis affirm God's eternal justice and favor. Let's see how he refutes these claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the two-part Arabic passage carefully, focusing on the structure of each objection and response.
Notice the phrase 'سؤال يلزم الأشعري' which indicates the objection applies to Ash'aris.
2
Identify the two objections
The first objection is about justice (عدل), the second about favor (تَفَضُّل). Both argue that if these attributes are not eternal, then God would have their opposites.
3
Understand the Maturidi response
Maturidi response: 'According to us, He was described with justice in pre-eternity' and similarly for favor. Therefore the objection does not apply.
This shows that Maturidis consider attributes of action as eternal.
4
Reflect on the Ash'ari implication
Note that the objection only targets the Ash'ari who deny these attributes in pre-eternity. It does not affect the Maturidi position.
This is a key theological distinction between the two Sunni schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يزعمون أن الله تعالى لا يستحيل أن يوصف بكونه عادلا ثم في الأزل كان غير موصوف به ولم يلزم اتصافه بضده وهو الجور. سؤال يلزم الأشعري لمطابقتهم إياه على انتفاء صفات الفعل في الأزل فأما علينا فغير لازم، لأنه تعالى عندنا كان في الأزل موصوفا بالعدل.
وكذا ما يزعمون أنه تعالى لو لم يكن في الأزل متفضلا لكان بخيلا من هذا القبيل. فإنه عندنا في الأزل كان متفضلا، وإنما يتوجه هذا السؤال على الأشعري (١).
وما يزعمون أن القادر على الكلام في الشاهد يتعرى عن الكلام وأضداده في حالة ثبوت القدرة. فشيء يبنونه على أصلهم في ادعائهم سبق القدرة على المقدور فأما عندنا فالقدرة على الكلام، مقترنة بالكلام فلا يتصور التعري عنه مع وجوده، وقبل وجود القدرة كان ضدا من أضداد الكلام ثابتا .
ثم يقال لهم : هذا أيضا على أصلكم فاسد ، فإن عندكم القدرة على الكلام، إن كانت منافية للآفة فهي غير منافية للسكوت، بل الساكت عندكم (۳) قادر على الكلام، وهذا لأن القدرة على أحد المتضادين عندكم لا تضاد ضد مقدوره، كما في قدرة الحركة والسكون ، وقدرة الكفر والإيمان (۳) وأشباه ذلك (٤). وبالله التوفيق.
And what they claim that Allah, exalted, is not impossible to be described as just, then in pre-eternity He was not described with it, and it does not necessitate His being described with its opposite, which is injustice. This is a question that necessarily applies to the Ash'ari because they agree with them [the Ash'ari] on the negation of attributes of action in pre-eternity. As for us, it is not necessary, because according to us, He, exalted, was described with justice in pre-eternity.
And likewise what they claim that He, exalted, if He were not in pre-eternity bestowing favor, He would be miserly — this is of the same kind. For according to us, He was bestowing favor in pre-eternity. This question only applies to the Ash'ari (1).
And what they claim that the one who is capable of speech in the empirical world becomes devoid of speech and its opposites when the ability is established. This is something they build on their principle that ability precedes the act. But according to us, the ability for speech is concurrent with speech, so being devoid of speech with its existence cannot be conceived. And before the existence of the ability, an opposite of the opposites of speech was established.
Then it is said to them: This also, according to your principle, is corrupt. For according to you, the ability for speech, if it is incompatible with impairment, it is not incompatible with silence. Rather, the silent one, according to you (3), is capable of speech. This is because the ability for one of two opposites, according to you, does not oppose the opposite of its object of ability, as in the ability for motion and rest, and the ability for unbelief and faith (3), and similar things (4). And by Allah is success.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of several objections raised by opponents against the Maturidi view of God's attributes in pre-eternity. The author first addresses the claim that if God is just, then in pre-eternity He would have to be described as just, but they argue that His attributes are not eternal. The author responds that this objection only applies to the Ash'ari who negate attributes of action in pre-eternity, whereas for Maturidis, God is eternally just. Similarly, the objection about favor (tafaddul) is rejected because God is eternally bestowing favor. Then the objection about the ability to speak: the opponents argue that if someone is capable of speech, they can be devoid of speech and its opposites. This is based on their principle that ability precedes the act. The author counters that for Maturidis, ability is concurrent with the act, so God is never devoid of speech. Furthermore, he turns the objection back on the opponents: according to their own principle, ability for speech is not incompatible with silence, as they hold that the silent person is still capable of speech, analogous to ability for motion and rest. Thus their own view is inconsistent. This passage shows the Maturidi commitment to eternal attributes and the necessary concurrence of ability and act.

Key Terms
عدل
جور
تَفَضُّل
بخيل
أزل
صفات الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidis and Ash'aris agree that attributes of action are not eternal.
Correction: Maturidis affirm that attributes like justice and favor are eternal in God's essence, while Ash'aris consider them temporal.

Checkpoint

A) Yes, always.
B) No, only after creation.
C) Only Ash'aris say yes.
D) It is impossible.

Key Takeaway
Maturidis affirm that God's attributes of action, such as justice and favor, are eternal in pre-eternity, contrary to the Ash'ari view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's justice is eternal and unchanging from pre-eternity, how does that change the way you process moments where you feel life has been unfair to you? Are you willing to trust that His justice is more comprehensive than your immediate experience, and what would that trust look like practically today?
?
The Maturidi view says God has been bestowing favor from pre-eternity, before you ever existed. Does your sense of gratitude stem from this foundational truth, or do you only feel thankful when you see tangible blessings? How can you cultivate a heart that acknowledges God's eternal generosity even in times of apparent deprivation?
?
This passage draws a sharp line between what you believe about God's attributes and how you respond to theological objections. But beyond doctrine, how does knowing that God was always just and generous affect the way you approach Him in your prayers and your daily decisions? Are you living as if His character is truly unchanging, or do your actions imply doubt?

Refuting the Objection on God's Ability to Speak in Pre-Eternity
Nasafi refutes the objection that God could be devoid of speech in pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidis argue that God's ability to speak is concurrent with speech itself, and why the opponents' objection is self-defeating.

Core Idea
For Maturidis, ability and act are simultaneous, so God is never without speech.

The third objection in this passage deals with God's ability to speak. Opponents claim that a person capable of speech can be without speech, so by analogy God could be without speech in pre-eternity. Nasafi refutes this by first stating the Maturidi principle that ability is concurrent with its act, and then turning the objection back on the opponents, showing that according to their own principles, silence does not negate the ability to speak. Let's examine this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the full passage on speech ability, including both the objection and the rebuttal.
2
Identify the objection
The objection says: in the empirical world, a person with the ability to speak can be devoid of speech and its opposites. So it seems possible for God to be without speech in pre-eternity.
The opponent relies on the principle that ability precedes the act.
3
Understand the Maturidi response
Nasafi responds: for us, the ability for speech is concurrent with speech, so being devoid of speech with existence of the ability is inconceivable. Before ability exists, silence is present.
This shows Maturidi view that ability does not precede the act but is simultaneous.
4
Follow the counter-argument
Nasafi then turns the objection: according to the opponent's own principle, ability for speech is not incompatible with silence, as the silent person is still capable of speech. So the objection backfires.
He draws an analogy with ability for motion and rest, and faith and disbelief.
5
Reflect on the implication
Thus the opponent's own view leads to inconsistency, and the objection against Maturidis is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يزعمون أن الله تعالى لا يستحيل أن يوصف بكونه عادلا ثم في الأزل كان غير موصوف به ولم يلزم اتصافه بضده وهو الجور. سؤال يلزم الأشعري لمطابقتهم إياه على انتفاء صفات الفعل في الأزل فأما علينا فغير لازم، لأنه تعالى عندنا كان في الأزل موصوفا بالعدل.
وكذا ما يزعمون أنه تعالى لو لم يكن في الأزل متفضلا لكان بخيلا من هذا القبيل. فإنه عندنا في الأزل كان متفضلا، وإنما يتوجه هذا السؤال على الأشعري (١).
وما يزعمون أن القادر على الكلام في الشاهد يتعرى عن الكلام وأضداده في حالة ثبوت القدرة. فشيء يبنونه على أصلهم في ادعائهم سبق القدرة على المقدور فأما عندنا فالقدرة على الكلام، مقترنة بالكلام فلا يتصور التعري عنه مع وجوده، وقبل وجود القدرة كان ضدا من أضداد الكلام ثابتا .
ثم يقال لهم : هذا أيضا على أصلكم فاسد ، فإن عندكم القدرة على الكلام، إن كانت منافية للآفة فهي غير منافية للسكوت، بل الساكت عندكم (۳) قادر على الكلام، وهذا لأن القدرة على أحد المتضادين عندكم لا تضاد ضد مقدوره، كما في قدرة الحركة والسكون ، وقدرة الكفر والإيمان (۳) وأشباه ذلك (٤). وبالله التوفيق.
And what they claim that Allah, exalted, is not impossible to be described as just, then in pre-eternity He was not described with it, and it does not necessitate His being described with its opposite, which is injustice. This is a question that necessarily applies to the Ash'ari because they agree with them [the Ash'ari] on the negation of attributes of action in pre-eternity. As for us, it is not necessary, because according to us, He, exalted, was described with justice in pre-eternity.
And likewise what they claim that He, exalted, if He were not in pre-eternity bestowing favor, He would be miserly — this is of the same kind. For according to us, He was bestowing favor in pre-eternity. This question only applies to the Ash'ari (1).
And what they claim that the one who is capable of speech in the empirical world becomes devoid of speech and its opposites when the ability is established. This is something they build on their principle that ability precedes the act. But according to us, the ability for speech is concurrent with speech, so being devoid of speech with its existence cannot be conceived. And before the existence of the ability, an opposite of the opposites of speech was established.
Then it is said to them: This also, according to your principle, is corrupt. For according to you, the ability for speech, if it is incompatible with impairment, it is not incompatible with silence. Rather, the silent one, according to you (3), is capable of speech. This is because the ability for one of two opposites, according to you, does not oppose the opposite of its object of ability, as in the ability for motion and rest, and the ability for unbelief and faith (3), and similar things (4). And by Allah is success.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of several objections raised by opponents against the Maturidi view of God's attributes in pre-eternity. The author first addresses the claim that if God is just, then in pre-eternity He would have to be described as just, but they argue that His attributes are not eternal. The author responds that this objection only applies to the Ash'ari who negate attributes of action in pre-eternity, whereas for Maturidis, God is eternally just. Similarly, the objection about favor (tafaddul) is rejected because God is eternally bestowing favor. Then the objection about the ability to speak: the opponents argue that if someone is capable of speech, they can be devoid of speech and its opposites. This is based on their principle that ability precedes the act. The author counters that for Maturidis, ability is concurrent with the act, so God is never devoid of speech. Furthermore, he turns the objection back on the opponents: according to their own principle, ability for speech is not incompatible with silence, as they hold that the silent person is still capable of speech, analogous to ability for motion and rest. Thus their own view is inconsistent. This passage shows the Maturidi commitment to eternal attributes and the necessary concurrence of ability and act.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ability always precedes the act.
Correction: In Maturidi theology, ability is simultaneous with the act, especially for God.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi view in this passage, when does the ability for speech exist relative to speech?
A) Before speech.
B) Concurrent with speech.
C) After speech.
D) It does not matter.

Key Takeaway
Maturidis hold that God's ability to speak is eternally concurrent with His speech, and the objection that He could be silent is invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe that Allah speaks eternally, but do you treat the Qur'an as His eternal speech or just a book from the past? If you truly believed that Allah is always speaking, would you give the Qur'an more attention and reverence in your daily life? How will you change your relationship with the Qur'an from today?
?
When you have the ability to do a good deed, do you postpone it? The lesson shows that for Allah, ability and act are concurrent. While that is unique to Him, it calls you to examine your own tendency to separate ability from action. What good deed have you been delaying that you will commit to doing today?

Why Muteness and Silence Are Opposites of Speech
Refutes objections to the Maturidi definition of divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why muteness and silence are considered opposites of speech in the context of divine attributes, and how the Maturidi school refutes objections that rely on physical organs.

Core Idea
Opposition is about incompatibility, not physical organ dependency.

The earlier lesson established the Maturidi position that God's speech is an eternal attribute, not dependent on organs. Here, Sanusi addresses common objections that try to equate speech with physical articulation. The objector argues that muteness is not an opposite because it is a deprivation, and silence is just non-use of an organ. This lesson walks through the refutation, clarifying that true opposition is logical incompatibility, not physical mechanics.

Guided Path
1
Examine the objector's initial claims
Read the objector's comparison of speech to chronic illness and his claim that silence is merely abstaining from using the speech organ. Notice how he uses the impossibility of organs for God to deny that God can be described as silent.
The objector cites a hadith about 'what the Quran is silent about' to support his view.
2
Follow Sanusi's forced-choice refutation on muteness
Sanusi asks: 'Do you affirm that muteness contradicts speech?' If the objector says no, he must allow speech and muteness to coexist (absurd). If yes, he admits they are opposites. This shows that the objector cannot deny opposition without absurdity.
Even if not a proper opposite, muteness is a 'preventing factor' (mani') that blocks speech.
3
Understand the shift from organ-based to meaning-based definitions
The core refutation: speech, muteness, and silence are defined by meanings (ma'ani) that are mutually exclusive, not by physical organs. Since God can be described with speech without organs, muteness and silence are also meanings that contradict speech, applicable even without physical organs.
The parallel with sight and hearing reinforces this: if they required organs, God could not be described as seeing, but He is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام، كالزمانة ليست بضد للفعل، وبخروجه من أن يكون فاعلا لم يلزم أن يكون زمنا، والسكوت ترك استعمال آلة الكلام، والله تعالى يستحيل عليه الآلة فيستحيل وصفه بأنه ساكت قال على أن عند بعض أصحابنا يجوز وصف الله تعالى بأنه ساكت قبل أن يتكلم ، وقد روي عن النبي عليه السلام أنه قال: "ما سكت عنه القرآن فهو عفو". الرد على اعتراضه فيجاب عن هذا الاعتراض فيقال: هل تقر أن الخرس ينافي الكلام؟ فإن قال: لا بَانَ ،بهته، وكلف أن يجوز اجتماع الكلام والخرس وإن قال : هو ينافي الكلام. فهذا هو الإقرار بكونهما متضادين وكذا الزمانة عندنا ضد الفعل لما قررنا، والاستشهاد بالزمانة إنما يستقيم له على الأشعرية لا علينا على أنه إن كان لا يسمى ضدا فلا شك أنه مانع، فيمتنع وجود الكلام عند وجوده عن من لا يستحيل اتصافه بالكلام، وعند ارتفاعه وارتفاع السكوت يجب وجود الكلام على ما قررنا. وكذا ما ذكر أن السكوت ليس بضد للكلام ، ويجاب عنه بما ذكر في فصل الخرس، ثم يقال له تنفصل ممن يقول لك : إن الكلام هو استعمال آلة الكلام، كما أن السكوت ترك استعمال آلة الكلام، والخرس آفة في آلة الكلام، والله سبحانه وتعالى يستحيل عليه الخرس والسكوت لاستحالة ثبوت الآلة له، فكذا يستحيل عليه الاتصاف بالكلام لاستحالة كونه ذا آلة وحيث جاز الاتصاف بالكلام مع استحالة الآلة دل أن الكلام ما كان كلاما لأنه استعمال الآلة بالنطق بل لأنه معنى ينافي السكوت والآفة، فكذا الخرس ما كان خرسا لأنه فساد في آلة النطق، بل لأنه آفة منافية للكلام، والسكوت ما كان سكوتا لأنه ترك استعمال آلة الكلام، بل لأنه معنى ينافي للكلام ممن يصح أن يوصف بالكلام، فإذا كان الكلام بالآلة كان السكوت بالآلة وإن كان الكلام لا بالأدلة فكذا كان السكوت لا بالآلة وكذا بم ينفصل ممن يقول البصر صحة الآلة وكذا السمع فمن الآلة كان سميعا بصيرا، ومن لا فلا والله تعالى يستحيل عليه الآلة صحيح فيستحيل أن يكون سميعا بصيرا، ويعتمد في ذلك مطلق الوجود كما فعلت أنت؟ فبأي جواب أجبت فهو جواي لك.
Speech, like chronic illness is not opposite to act, and by his being not an agent it does not necessitate that he be chronically ill. Silence is abandoning the use of the organ of speech, and Allah Almighty is impossible of having an organ, so it is impossible to describe Him as silent. Moreover, some of our companions allow describing Allah Almighty as silent before He speaks, and it has been narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'What the Quran is silent about is pardoned.' Refutation of his objection: So this objection is answered by saying: Do you affirm that muteness contradicts speech? If he says no, his falsehood becomes clear, and he is required to allow the combination of speech and muteness. And if he says that it contradicts speech, then this is an admission that they are opposites. Similarly, chronic illness according to us is opposite to act as we established. The citation of chronic illness is valid only against the Ash'aris, not against us. Even if it is not called an opposite, it is undoubtedly a preventing factor; so the existence of speech is impossible at its existence from one for whom description with speech is not impossible. And at its removal and the removal of silence, the existence of speech becomes necessary as we established. Likewise, what was mentioned that silence is not opposite to speech is answered by what was mentioned in the chapter on muteness. Then it is said to him: You are refuted by one who says to you: Speech is the use of the organ of speech, just as silence is abandoning the use of the organ of speech, and muteness is a defect in the organ of speech. Allah Almighty is impossible of having muteness and silence because of the impossibility of an organ for Him. Thus, it is also impossible for Him to be described with speech because of the impossibility of His being possessor of an organ. And since description with speech is allowed despite the impossibility of an organ, it indicates that speech was not called speech because it is the use of the organ through articulation, but rather because it is a meaning that contradicts silence and defect. Similarly, muteness was not called muteness because it is a corruption in the organ of articulation, but rather because it is a defect that contradicts speech. And silence was not called silence because it is abandoning the use of the organ of speech, but rather because it is a meaning that contradicts speech from one who can be described with speech. If speech is by organ, then silence is by organ, and if speech is not by organs, then silence is also not by organ. Similarly, he is refuted by one who says: Sight is soundness of the organ, and similarly hearing. So one who has an organ is hearing and seeing, and one who does not is not. Allah Almighty is impossible of having an organ, so it is impossible that He be hearing and seeing. And you rely on absolute existence as you did? By whatever answer you answer, it is my answer to you.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection against the Maturidi position on God's attribute of speech. The objector begins by comparing speech to chronic illness (zamanah), claiming that just as chronic illness is not truly opposite to an act (since it is not a voluntary action), muteness (khars) is not truly opposite to speech. He also argues that silence (sukt) is merely the non-use of the speech organ, and since God cannot have an organ, He cannot be described as silent. The objector then cites a hadith: 'What the Quran is silent about is pardoned.' The author then provides the refutation. First, he questions the objector: 'Do you affirm that muteness contradicts speech?' If the objector denies it, he is refuted because he would then have to allow the coexistence of speech and muteness (which is absurd). If he admits it, he has conceded that they are opposites. The author then addresses the analogy with chronic illness, stating that even if it is not called a proper opposite, it is a preventing factor (mani'), meaning that speech cannot exist when muteness is present. Regarding silence, the author says it is answered similarly. The core of the argument then shifts: the objector claims speech is use of an organ, but the author counters that speech is a meaning (ma'na) that contradicts silence and defect, not dependent on organs. Therefore, the inability to attribute organs to God does not negate His speech; rather, it necessitates that speech be understood as a meaning. The author then addresses the analogous case of sight and hearing: if the objector says sight requires an organ, then God cannot be seeing. But the Maturidi position is that God is seeing and hearing without organs. So the objector's reliance on 'absolute existence' (mujarrad al-wujud) is inconsistent. The author concludes that whatever answer the objector gives to this analogy, the same answer applies to his own objection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Muteness is not opposite to speech because it is a deprivation, not an active state.
Correction: Muteness is a preventing factor (mani') that makes speech impossible; opposition is about mutual exclusion, not about being an active state.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what makes muteness (khars) opposite to speech?
A) Muteness is a defect in the organ of speech.
B) Muteness is incompatible with the existence of speech.
C) Muteness is a kind of silence.
D) The Quran explicitly states so.

Key Takeaway
Muteness and silence are opposites of speech because they are logically incompatible with its existence, not because of any physical organ requirement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objector considered silence as merely the non-use of an organ. Have you ever justified your own silence about a truth by calling it a mere absence of action? How does this lesson's insistence that silence is a positive contradiction of speech challenge your excuses?
?
If God's speech is not dependent on any organ, what does that imply about the eternal nature of the Quran? Does your daily interaction with the Quran reflect this eternal, uncreated reality, or do you treat it as a human book?
